## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on P through density-dependent feedback mechanisms, and may depend on t through seasonal or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (growth decelerating logarithmically near capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (scale-free population growth)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth minus death)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density feedback)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with saturating harvest)
- Delayed feedback proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (logistic with time-varying capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent exponential growth regime
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P^2) indicates pairwise competition or logistic-type density dependence
- Cubic terms in P (P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicate strong Allee effects with a minimum viable population
- Logarithmic dependence on P (P*log(K/P)) indicates Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically
- Ratio-dependent terms P/(1+c*P) indicate saturating interactions such as limited resources or predator functional responses
- Trigonometric dependence on t (sin(c*t)) indicates seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where 0<c<1) indicate surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Product of P with a decreasing function of P ensures self-limiting growth and finite carrying capacity
- Explicit time dependence beyond periodic forcing may indicate non-autonomous dynamics such as habitat degradation or climate trends
- Sign changes in dP_dt as P increases indicate equilibrium points (stable or unstable) in population dynamics

## Analysis

$$f(t,P) = 0.11782 \cdot (1 - e^{-0.02723P}) \cdot P + 0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723t}$$

Expanding the first term:
$$f(t,P) = 0.11782 \cdot P - 0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723P} + 0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723t}$$

This has three terms:
1. A term proportional to $P$
2. A term proportional to $P \cdot e^{-0.02723P}$ (i.e., $P \cdot \exp(cP)$ with negative constant)
3. A term proportional to $P \cdot e^{-0.02723t}$ (i.e., $P \cdot \exp(ct)$ with negative constant)

So the GT = $0.11782 \cdot P + (-0.11782) \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723 \cdot P} + 0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723 \cdot t}$

Now looking at **Candidate 6**: $P \cdot c_0 \cdot \exp(P \cdot c_1) + P \cdot c_2 \cdot \exp(c_3 \cdot t) + P \cdot c_4$

This has exactly three terms:
- $P \cdot c_4$ → matches $0.11782 \cdot P$ with $c_4 = 0.11782$
- $P \cdot c_0 \cdot \exp(P \cdot c_1)$ → matches $-0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723P}$ with $c_0 = -0.11782$, $c_1 = -0.02723$
- $P \cdot c_2 \cdot \exp(c_3 \cdot t)$ → matches $0.11782 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.02723t}$ with $c_2 = 0.11782$, $c_3 = -0.02723$

**Candidate 6 matches the GT exactly** with:
- $c_0 = -0.11782$
- $c_1 = -0.02723$
- $c_2 = 0.11782$
- $c_3 = -0.02723$
- $c_4 = 0.11782$

Many other candidates (8, 9, 11, 13, 35, etc.) also contain Candidate 6 as a subset (with extra terms that can be zeroed out), but Candidate 6 is the simplest exact match.

Conclusion: Match found
